1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div></div></div></div><h3 id="docker-compose-troubleshooting" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Docker Compose troubleshooting<a class="headerlink" href="#docker-compose-troubleshooting" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>If you encounter connection issues:</p><ol><li>Ensure all containers are running: <code>docker-compose ps</code></li><li>Check container logs: <code>docker-compose logs kafka</code></li><li>Ensure the bootstrap servers address in your Connection file matches the <code>KAFKA_ADVERTISED_LISTENERS</code> value in your <code>docker-compose.yml</code> file.</li></ol><h2 id="kafka-meta-columns" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Kafka meta columns<a class="headerlink" href="#kafka-meta-columns" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>When you connect a data source to Kafka, the following columns are added to store metadata from Kafka messages:</p><div class="max-w-[calc(100%_+_40px)] overflow-auto -mx-5 ps-5 md:max-w-full md:mx-0 md:ps-0"><table><thead><tr><th>name</th><th>type</th><th>description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>__value </code></td><td><code>String</code></td><td>A String representing the entire unparsed value of the Kafka message. It is only populated if <code>KAFKA_STORE_RAW_VALUE</code> is set to <code>True</code>.</td></tr><tr><td><code>__topic </code></td><td><code>LowCardinality(String)</code></td><td>The topic that the message was read from.</td></tr><tr><td><code>__partition </code></td><td><code>Int16</code></td><td>The partition that the message was read from.</td></tr><tr><td><code>__offset </code></td><td><code>Int16</code></td><td>The offset of the message.</td></tr><tr><td><code>__timestamp </code></td><td><code>Datetime</code></td><td>The timestamp of the message.</td></tr><tr><td><code>__key </code></td><td><code>String</code></td><td>The key of the message.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><p>Optionally, when <code>KAFKA_STORE_HEADERS</code> is set to <code>True</code>, the following column is added and populated:</p><div class="max-w-[calc(100%_+_40px)] overflow-auto -mx-5 ps-5 md:max-w-full md:mx-0 md:ps-0"><table><thead><tr><th>name</th><th>type</th><th>description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>__headers</code></td><td><code>Map(String, String)</code></td><td>Kafka headers of the message.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-info text-code"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M7.86 9.742a1 1 0 0 0-.08.1.5.5 0 0 0-.06.12.4.4 0 0 0-.04.12 1 1 0 0 0 0 .134.56.56 0 0 0 .053.253.6.6 0 0 0 .36.36.63.63 0 0 0 .507 0 .6.6 0 0 0 .36-.36.7.7 0 0 0 .04-.253.667.667 0 0 0-1.14-.474m.473-8.86a6.667 6.667 0 1 0 0 13.334 6.667 6.667 0 0 0 0-13.334m0 12a5.333 5.333 0 1 1 0-10.666 5.333 5.333 0 0 1 0 10.666m0-8.666a2 2 0 0 0-1.733 1 .667.667 0 1 0 1.153.666.667.667 0 0 1 1.052-.138.667.667 0 0 1-.472 1.138.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v.667a.667.667 0 0 0 1.333 0v-.12a2 2 0 0 0-.667-3.88"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>When you iterate your Kafka data source, you might need to use the meta columns in the<!-- --> <a href="/docs/forward/test-and-deploy/evolve-data-source#forward-query">FORWARD_QUERY</a>. Tinybird suggests a valid forward query that you can tweak to get the desired values for each column.</p></div></div><h2 id="kafka-logs" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Kafka logs<a class="headerlink" href="#kafka-logs" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><article><p>You can find global logs in the <code>datasources_ops_log</code> <a href="/docs/forward/monitoring/service-datasources#tinybird-datasources-ops-log">Service Data Source</a>. Filter by <code>datasource_id</code> to select the correct datasource, and by <code>event_type=&#x27;append-kafka&#x27;</code>.</p><p>For example, to select all Kafka releated logs in the last day, run the following query:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT *
FROM tinybird.datasources_ops_log
WHERE datasource_id = &#x27;t_1234&#x27;
  AND event_type = &#x27;append-kafka&#x27;
  AND timestamp &gt; now() - INTERVAL 1 day
ORDER BY timestamp DESC
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>If you can&#x27;t find logs in <code>datasources_ops_log</code>, the <code>kafka_ops_log</code> <a href="/docs/forward/monitoring/service-datasources#tinybird-kafka-ops-log">Service Data Source</a> contains more detailed logs. Filter by <code>datasource_id</code> to select the correct datasource, and use <code>msg_type</code> to select the desired log level (<code>info</code>, <code>warning</code>, or <code>error</code>).</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT *
FROM tinybird.kafka_ops_log
WHERE datasource_id = &#x27;t_1234&#x27;
  AND timestamp &gt; now() - interval 1 day
  AND msg_type IN [&#x27;info&#x27;, &#x27;warning&#x27;, &#x27;error&#x27;]
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-caution text-[#856100]"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M8.333 10.216a.666.666 0 1 0 0 1.332.666.666 0 0 0 0-1.332m7.114.98L10.08 1.862a2 2 0 0 0-3.493 0l-5.334 9.334a2 2 0 0 0 1.707 3.02h10.747a2 2 0 0 0 1.74-3.02m-1.154 1.333a.67.67 0 0 1-.586.34H2.96a.67.67 0 0 1-.587-.34.67.67 0 0 1 0-.667L7.707 2.53a.667.667 0 0 1 1.186 0l5.367 9.333a.67.67 0 0 1 .033.68zm-5.96-7.647a.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v2.667a.667.667 0 1 0 1.333 0V5.549a.667.667 0 0 0-.667-.667"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>When your Data Source encounters a high rate of specific Kafka connection errors, we temporarily stop ingestion for exponentially increasing periods of time. This mechanism is called a Circuit Breaker. It prevents polluting your logs and our system and is only activated by the errors listed in <a href="#kafka-circuit-breaker-errors">this section</a>.</p><p>For example, if your Kafka brokers are unreachable, you will see a message in your logs similar to this: &quot;We have opened a circuit breaker because your error rate is too high. Please, fix your connection and if you think everything is fine, contact support.&quot;</p><p>If the connection issue persists through all retries, ingestion will be paused. Once you fix the underlying connection problem, the Circuit Breaker resets, and ingestion will resume from where it left off.</p></div></div><h3 id="kafka-circuit-breaker-errors" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Kafka circuit breaker errors<a class="headerlink" href="#kafka-circuit-breaker-errors" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>The following Kafka errors trigger the Circuit Breaker</p><div class="max-w-[calc(100%_+_40px)] overflow-auto -mx-5 ps-5 md:max-w-full md:mx-0 md:ps-0"><table><thead><tr><th>Error</th><th>Error message</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>_ALL_BROKERS_DOWN</code></td><td>Local: All broker connections are down</td></tr><tr><td><code>_TRANSPORT</code></td><td>Local: Broker transport failure</td></tr><tr><td><code>_TIMED_OUT</code></td><td>Local: Timed out</td></tr><tr><td><code>_DESTROY</code></td><td>Local: Broker handle destroyed</td></tr><tr><td><code>_AUTHENTICATION</code></td><td>Local: Authentication failure</td></tr><tr><td><code>_RESOLVE</code></td><td>Local: Host resolution failure</td></tr><tr><td><code>_UNKNOWN_TOPIC</code></td><td>Local: Unknown topic</td></tr><tr><td><code>_UNKNOWN_PARTITION</code></td><td>Local: Unknown partition</td></tr><tr><td><code>SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED</code></td><td>Broker: SASL Authentication failed</td></tr><tr><td><code>TOPIC_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED</code></td><td>Broker: Topic authorization failed</td></tr><tr><td><code>GROUP_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED</code></td><td>Broker: Group authorization failed</td></tr><tr><td><code>CLUSTER_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED</code></td><td>Broker: Cluster authorization failed</td></tr></tbody></table></div></article><p>For comprehensive monitoring of your Kafka connectors, including lag tracking, throughput analysis, and error monitoring, see <a href="/docs/forward/monitoring/kafka-clickhouse-monitoring">Monitor Kafka connectors</a>.</p><h2 id="pause-and-resume-ingestion" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Pause and resume ingestion<a class="headerlink" href="#pause-and-resume-ingestion" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>In branches and Tinybird Local, you can pause and resume Kafka ingestion using the CLI:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">tb [--branch=BRANCH_NAME] datasource stop my_kafka_datasource
tb [--branch=BRANCH_NAME] datasource start my_kafka_datasource
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Stopping a Data Source pauses ingestion from the Kafka topic. When you start it again, the behavior depends on the environment. In branches, a new consumer group is created and ingestion starts from the latest offset. In Tinybird Local, ingestion resumes from the last committed offset.</p><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-info text-code"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M7.86 9.742a1 1 0 0 0-.08.1.5.5 0 0 0-.06.12.4.4 0 0 0-.04.12 1 1 0 0 0 0 .134.56.56 0 0 0 .053.253.6.6 0 0 0 .36.36.63.63 0 0 0 .507 0 .6.6 0 0 0 .36-.36.7.7 0 0 0 .04-.253.667.667 0 0 0-1.14-.474m.473-8.86a6.667 6.667 0 1 0 0 13.334 6.667 6.667 0 0 0 0-13.334m0 12a5.333 5.333 0 1 1 0-10.666 5.333 5.333 0 0 1 0 10.666m0-8.666a2 2 0 0 0-1.733 1 .667.667 0 1 0 1.153.666.667.667 0 0 1 1.052-.138.667.667 0 0 1-.472 1.138.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v.667a.667.667 0 0 0 1.333 0v-.12a2 2 0 0 0-.667-3.88"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>Because each start creates a new consumer group, previous consumer groups become orphaned. Depending on your Kafka cluster&#x27;s consumer group TTL (<code>offsets.retention.minutes</code>), these orphan groups may persist until they expire.</p></div></div><p>See <a href="/docs/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-datasource#tb-datasource-start">tb datasource start</a> and <a href="/docs/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-datasource#tb-datasource-stop">tb datasource stop</a> for more details.</p><h2 id="troubleshooting" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Troubleshooting<a class="headerlink" href="#troubleshooting" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>For comprehensive troubleshooting guidance, see the <a href="kafka/troubleshooting">Kafka connector troubleshooting guide</a>.</p><p>Common issues include:</p><ul><li>Connection timeout or broker unreachable</li><li>Authentication failures</li><li>SSL/TLS certificate validation errors</li><li>Deserialization errors (Avro, JSON)</li><li>Offset and consumer group conflicts</li><li>Consumer lag issues</li><li>Schema mismatches</li></ul><p>Each combination of <code>KAFKA_TOPIC</code> and <code>KAFKA_GROUP_ID</code> can only be used in one data source,<!-- --> <!-- -->otherwise the offsets committed by the consumers of different data sources clash.</p><p>If you connect a data source to Kafka using a <code>KAFKA_TOPIC</code> and <code>KAFKA_GROUP_ID</code> that were<!-- --> <!-- -->previously used by another data source in your workspace, the data source only receives data<!-- --> <!-- -->from the last committed offset, even if <code>KAFKA_AUTO_OFFSET_RESET</code> is set to <code>earliest</code>.</p><p>To prevent these issues, always use unique <code>KAFKA_GROUP_ID</code>s when testing Kafka data sources.</p><p>See <a href="#kafka-logs">Kafka logs</a> to learn how to diagnose any other issues</p><h3 id="compressed-messages" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Compressed messages<a class="headerlink" href="#compressed-messages" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Tinybird can consume from Kafka topics where Kafka compression is turned on; decompressing the<!-- --> <!-- -->message is a standard function of the Kafka consumer. However, if you compressed the message before passing it through the Kafka producer, Tinybird can&#x27;t do post-consumer processing to decompress the message.</p><p>For example, if you compressed a JSON message through gzip and produced it to a Kafka topic as a<!-- --> <code>bytes</code> message, it would be ingested by Tinybird as <code>bytes</code>. If you produced a JSON message to a<!-- --> <!-- -->Kafka topic with the Kafka producer setting <code>compression.type=gzip</code>, while it would be stored in<!-- --> <!-- -->Kafka as compressed bytes, it would be decoded on ingestion and arrive to Tinybird as JSON.</p><h2 id="connecting-an-existing-data-source-to-kafka" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Connecting an existing data source to Kafka<a class="headerlink" href="#connecting-an-existing-data-source-to-kafka" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>You can connect an existing, default data source to Kafka.</p><p>Create the Kafka .connection file if it does not exist, add the desired Kafka settings to the .datasource file, and add a <a href="/docs/forward/test-and-deploy"><code>FORWARD_QUERY</code></a> to provide default values for the <a href="#kafka-meta-columns">Kafka meta columns</a>.</p><h2 id="disconnecting-a-data-source-from-kafka" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Disconnecting a data source from Kafka<a class="headerlink" href="#disconnecting-a-data-source-from-kafka" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>To disconnect a data source from Kafka, remove the Kafka settings from the .datasource file.</p><p>If you want to keep any of the <a href="#kafka-meta-columns">Kafka meta columns</a>, add them to the schema with a default value and adjust the <code>FORWARD_QUERY</code> accordingly.</p><h2 id="additional-resources" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Additional resources<a class="headerlink" href="#additional-resources" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><h3 id="guides" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Guides<a class="headerlink" href="#guides" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><a href="kafka/guides/confluent-cloud-setup">Confluent Cloud setup</a> - End-to-end setup for Confluent Cloud</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/aws-msk-setup">AWS MSK setup</a> - Complete MSK configuration guide</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/redpanda-setup">Redpanda setup</a> - Redpanda-specific configuration</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/local-development">Local development</a> - Local development setup and testing</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/cicd-version-control">CI/CD and version control</a> - Managing connections across environments</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/schema-management">Schema management</a> - Schema evolution and data type mapping</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/partitioning-strategies">Partitioning strategies</a> - Best practices for Kafka partitioning</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/message-size-handling">Message size handling</a> - Handling large messages and troubleshooting</li><li><a href="kafka/guides/performance-optimization">Performance optimization</a> - Throughput optimization and tuning</li></ul><h3 id="reference" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Reference<a class="headerlink" href="#reference" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><a href="kafka/troubleshooting">Troubleshooting guide</a> - Comprehensive error resolution with error lookup table</li><li><a href="kafka/limits">Limits and quotas</a> - Kafka connector limits and how to request increases</li></ul><h3 id="related-documentation" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Related documentation<a class="headerlink" href="#related-documentation" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><ul><li><a href="/docs/forward/monitoring/kafka-clickhouse-monitoring">Monitor Kafka connectors</a> - Monitoring queries and alerts</li><li><a href="/docs/forward/work-with-data/publish-data/sinks/kafka-sink">Kafka Sink</a> - Exporting data to Kafka</li><li><a href="/docs/forward/get-data-in/quarantine">Quarantine Data Sources</a> - Handling failed messages</li></ul></article><div class="flex items-center justify-end h-10" data-pagefind-ignore="true"><div class="italic text-caption"><span>Updated<!-- --> <time dateTime="2026-02-12T19:43:39.000Z">4 weeks ago</time></span></div></div><nav class="flex justify-between items-stretch gap-2 md:gap-4 mt-4 border-t border-v-border pt-8" data-pagefind-ignore="true"><div class="flex-1 flex items-stretch"><a href="/docs/forward/get-data-in/connectors" class="group flex items-stretch hover:no-underline flex-1"><div class="flex 8.1 9.795 11.454 6l.746.994z"></path></svg></div><div class="flex-1 flex flex-col justify-center p-2 md:p-4 rounded-lg border border-v-border hover:border-v-border-active hover:bg-v-bg-active"><span \"default\"]\n47:I[57187,[\"5878\",\"static/chunks/9da6db1e-fe3f3691e817470b.js\",\"314\",\"static/chunks/32ea55aa-334b9848c750da09.js\",\"4960\",\"static/chunks/8b30ef62-8e1a3557163ef34d.js\",\"9729\",\"static/chunks/72b2f85d-e46ed6c2f9c8d9d7.js\",\"5501\",\"static/chunks/c16f53c3-0400c7825a916970.js\",\"8370\",\"static/chunks/8370-7a9554878d1b9d35.js\",\"7648\",\"static/chunks/7648-2c0c3a3dc3702719.js\",\"2694\",\"static/chunks/2694-6ee008eb8be89699.js\",\"9267\",\"static/chunks/9267-89ff5dc708370f39.js\",\"1284\",\"static/chunks/1284-f30446673b9ba073.js\",\"7867\",\"static/chunks/7867-6d0484accd87a171.js\",\"3145\",\"static/chunks/3145-ca0c40eb1bb881d8.js\",\"5107\",\"static/chunks/5107-ef688f2fbbe55825.js\",\"2418\",\"static/chunks/2418-b0d27e6f47546ed6.js\",\"4144\",\"static/chunks/4144-34f98e6e70550e12.js\",\"1147\",\"static/chunks/1147-ac53c80b8f8a3921.js\",\"1749\",\"static/chunks/1749-b2df567f1b8974df.js\",\"5643\",\"static/chunks/5643-5ba78075e5c8bae2.js\",\"1796\",\"static/chunks/1796-b956fe6fe21dbf17.js\",\"787\",\"static/chunks/787-09fc1907ef45c351.js\",\"996\",\"static/chunks/996-ce0ceee74ea8f43a.js\",\"7432\",\"static/chunks/7432-03643de0998568d4.js\",\"1384\",\"static/chunks/app/(forward)/forward/%5B%5B...slug%5D%5D/page-8347ce85311902e7.js\"],\"default\"]\n21:T7503,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"---\ntitle: Kafka connector\nmeta:\n   description: Complete guide to setting up and configuring the Kafka connector for Tinybird. Connect to Kafka, Confluent Cloud, AWS MSK, Redpanda, and other Kafka-compatible platforms. Includes authentication, troubleshooting, and performance optimization.\n---\n\n# Kafka connector\n\nYou can set up a Kafka connector to consume data from a Kafka topic and store it in Tinybird by creating a [.connection](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles/connection-files) and [.datasource](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles/datasource-files) file. Use `tb datasource create --kafka` command for a guided the process.\n\n## Set up the connector\n\nTo set up the Kafka connector, follow these steps.\n\n{% steps %}\n\n### Create a Kafka connection\n\nYou can create a Kafka connection in Tinybird using either the CLI or by manually creating a connection file.\n\n#### Option 1: Use the CLI (recommended)\n\nRun the following command to create a connection:\n\n```bash\ntb connection create kafka\n```\n\nYou are prompted to enter:\n\n1. A name for your connection.\n2. The bootstrap server\n3. The Kafka key\n4. The Kafka secret\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nIf you need to add `KAFKA_SCHEMA_REGISTRY_URL` or any of the [Kafka .connection settings](#kafka-connection-settings), edit the .connection file manually.\n{% /callout %}\n\n#### Option 2: Manually create a connection file\n\nCreate a [.connection file](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles/connection-files) with the required credentials stored in secrets. Check [Kafka .connection settings](#kafka-connection-settings) for a complete list of Kafka connection settings.\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nSecrets are only replaced in your resources when you deploy. If you change a secret, you need to\ndeploy for the changes to take effect.\n{% /callout %}\n\n#### Authentication methods\n\nTinybird supports multiple authentication methods for Kafka connections:\n\n##### SASL/PLAIN\n\nThe most common authentication method for cloud Kafka providers like Confluent Cloud.\n\n```tb {% title=\"kafka_sasl_plain.connection\" %}\nTYPE kafka\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS \u003cBOOTSTRAP_SERVERS:PORT\u003e\nKAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL SASL_SSL\nKAFKA_SASL_MECHANISM PLAIN\nKAFKA_KEY {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_KEY\", \"key\") }}\nKAFKA_SECRET {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_SECRET\", \"secret\") }}\n```\n\nSet the kafka key and secret using [tb secret](/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-secret):\n\n```bash\ntb [--cloud] secret set KAFKA_KEY \u003cKAFKA_KEY\u003e\ntb [--cloud] secret set KAFKA_SECRET \u003cKAFKA_SECRET\u003e\n```\n\n##### SASL/SCRAM-SHA-256 or SCRAM-SHA-512\n\nFor Kafka clusters using SCRAM authentication:\n\n```tb {% title=\"kafka_sasl_scram.connection\" %}\nTYPE kafka\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS \u003cBOOTSTRAP_SERVERS:PORT\u003e\nKAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL SASL_SSL\nKAFKA_SASL_MECHANISM SCRAM-SHA-256\nKAFKA_KEY {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_KEY\", \"key\") }}\nKAFKA_SECRET {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_SECRET\", \"secret\") }}\n```\n\nReplace `SCRAM-SHA-256` with `SCRAM-SHA-512` if your cluster uses SHA-512.\n\n##### SASL/OAuthBearer (AWS MSK)\n\nFor AWS MSK clusters using IAM authentication:\n\n```tb {% title=\"kafka_sasl_oauthbearer_aws.connection\" %}\nTYPE kafka\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS \u003cBOOTSTRAP_SERVERS:PORT\u003e\nKAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL SASL_SSL\nKAFKA_SASL_MECHANISM OAUTHBEARER\nKAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_METHOD AWS\nKAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_AWS_REGION \u003cAWS_REGION\u003e\nKAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_AWS_ROLE_ARN {{ tb_secret(\"AWS_ROLE_ARN\") }}\nKAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_AWS_EXTERNAL_ID \u003cAWS_EXTERNAL_ID\u003e\n```\n\nWhen using AWS method, you need to set up the required AWS IAM role with appropriate permissions. See the [AWS IAM permissions](#aws-iam-permissions) section for details on the required access policy and trust policy configurations.\n\nSet the AWS role ARN using [tb secret](/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-secret):\n\n```bash\ntb [--cloud] secret set AWS_ROLE_ARN \u003cAWS_ROLE_ARN\u003e\n```\n\nFor detailed setup instructions for specific vendors, see:\n- [Confluent Cloud setup guide](kafka/guides/confluent-cloud-setup)\n- [AWS MSK setup guide](kafka/guides/aws-msk-setup)\n- [Redpanda setup guide](kafka/guides/redpanda-setup)\n\n##### PLAINTEXT (local development only)\n\nFor local development with unsecured Kafka:\n\n```tb {% title=\"kafka_plaintext.connection\" %}\nTYPE kafka\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS localhost:9092\nKAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL PLAINTEXT\n```\n\n{% callout type=\"warning\" %}\nPLAINTEXT connections are only suitable for local development. Production Kafka clusters should use SASL_SSL.\n{% /callout %}\n\nFor more information on local development setup, see the [local development guide](kafka/guides/local-development).\n\n### Bootstrap servers configuration\n\nThe `KAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS` setting specifies one or more Kafka brokers to connect to. Use comma-separated values for multiple brokers:\n\n```tb\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS broker1:9092,broker2:9092,broker3:9092\n```\n\n**Important considerations:**\n- Use the advertised listeners address, not the internal broker address\n- For cloud providers, use the public endpoint provided by your Kafka service\n- Ensure the port matches your security protocol (9092 for PLAINTEXT, 9093-9096 for SASL_SSL depending on provider)\n- For AWS MSK, use the bootstrap broker string from the MSK console\n\nIf you encounter connection issues, see the [troubleshooting guide](kafka/troubleshooting#error-connection-timeout-or-broker-unreachable) for bootstrap server configuration help.\n\n### SSL/TLS certificate configuration\n\nWhen using `SASL_SSL` security protocol, you may need to provide a CA certificate, especially for:\n- Self-signed certificates\n- Private CA certificates\n- Aiven Kafka (Private CA port)\n\nThe recommended way to provide the certificate is using secrets.\n\nCreate the multiline secret with the certificate using [tb secret](/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-secret#tb-secret-set). This opens an editor\nto introduce the value.\n\n```bash\ntb [--cloud] secret set --multiline KAFKA_PROD_SSL_CA_PEM\n```\n\nUse the secret in the `KAFKA_SSL_CA_PEM` setting of the connection file. Take into account this is a [multiline setting](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles#multiple-lines).\n\n```tb {% title=\"/connections/kafka_ssl_ca_pem.connection\" %}\nTYPE kafka\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SERVER\", \"kafka:29092\") }}\nKAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SECURITY_PROTOCOL\", \"PLAINTEXT\") }}\nKAFKA_SASL_MECHANISM {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SASL_MECHANISM\", \"PLAIN\") }}\nKAFKA_KEY {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_KEY\", \"key\") }}\nKAFKA_SECRET {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SECRET\", \"secret\") }}\nKAFKA_SSL_CA_PEM \u003e\n  {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SSL_CA_PEM\") }}\n```\n\n**Certificate format requirements:**\n- Certificate must be in PEM format (starts with `-----BEGIN CERTIFICATE-----`)\n- Include the full certificate chain if required\n- For Aiven Kafka, download the CA certificate from the Aiven console\n\nFor troubleshooting SSL certificate issues, see the [troubleshooting guide](kafka/troubleshooting#error-ssltls-certificate-validation-failed).\n\n### Create a Kafka data source\n\nCreate a .datasource file using `tb datasource create --kafka` or manually.\n\nDefine the data source schema as with any non-Kafka datasource and specify the required Kafka\nsettings. The value of `KAFKA_CONNECTION_NAME` must match the name of the .connection file\nyou created in the previous step.\n\nThe default .datasource stores the whole message in a column called `data`. Then, you can use [JSONExtract functions](/sql-reference/functions/json-functions#jsonextract-functions) to access the message fields, either at query time or using materialized views.\n\n```tb {% title=\"kafka_default.datasource\" %}\nSCHEMA \u003e\n    `data` String `json:$`\n\nKAFKA_CONNECTION_NAME kafka_connection # The name of the .connection file\nKAFKA_TOPIC topic_name\nKAFKA_GROUP_ID {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_GROUP_ID\") }}\n```\n\nYou can always use [JSONPaths](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles/datasource-files#jsonpath-expressions) syntax to extract the message fields into separate columns at ingest time.\n\n```tb {% title=\"kafka_sample.datasource\" %}\nSCHEMA \u003e\n   `timestamp` DateTime(3) `json:$.timestamp`,\n   `session_id` String `json:$.session_id`,\n   `action` LowCardinality(String) `json:$.action`,\n   `version` LowCardinality(String) `json:$.version`,\n   `payload` String `json:$.payload`,\n   `data` String `json:$`\n\nKAFKA_CONNECTION_NAME kafka_sample # The name of the .connection file\nKAFKA_TOPIC test_topic\nKAFKA_GROUP_ID {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_GROUP_ID\") }}\n```\n\nIn addition to the columns specified in `SCHEMA`, Kafka data sources have additional columns\nthat store metadata of the messages ingested. See [Kafka meta columns](#kafka-meta-columns) for more\ninformation.\n\nFor a complete list of Kafka data source settings, see [Kafka .datasource settings](#kafka-datasource-settings).\n\n{% callout type=\"caution\" %}\nUse different consumer group values for `KAFKA_GROUP_ID` at different environments to isolate consumers and their committed offset.\n{% /callout %}\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nIf you use [Kafka Tombstones](https://docs.confluent.io/kafka/design/log_compaction.html#compaction-enables-deletes), Tinybird sends these `null`-payload messages to the Quarantine Data Source if your Data Source's schema can't accept them. You can inspect the tombstone records without affecting your main Data Source.\n{% /callout %}\n\n### Connectivity check\n\nAfter defining your Kafka data source and connection, test the connection and preview data:\n\n```bash\ntb connection data \u003cconnection_name\u003e\n```\n\nThis command prompts you to:\n1. Select a Kafka topic\n2. Enter a consumer group ID\n3. Returns preview data from the topic\n\nThis validates that Tinybird can connect to your Kafka broker, authenticate, and consume messages. Remember to set any secrets used by the connection.\n\n{% /steps %}\n\n## Compatibility\n\nThe connector is compatible with Apache Kafka and works with any compatible implementation and vendor. The following are tried and tested:\n\n- Apache Kafka\n- Confluent Platform and Confluent Cloud Platform\n- Redpanda\n- AWS MSK\n- Azure Event Hubs for Apache Kafka\n- Estuary\n\nFor vendor-specific setup guides, see:\n- [Confluent Cloud setup](kafka/guides/confluent-cloud-setup)\n- [AWS MSK setup](kafka/guides/aws-msk-setup)\n- [Redpanda setup](kafka/guides/redpanda-setup)\n\n## Schema management and evolution\n\nTinybird supports multiple serialization formats for Kafka messages:\n\n- **JSON** (`json_without_schema` or `json_with_schema`)\n- **Avro** (requires Schema Registry)\n- **JSON Schema** (requires Schema Registry)\n\nWhen using Schema Registry, Tinybird automatically handles schema evolution for backward-compatible changes. For detailed information on schema management, including adding fields, handling nullable types, and data type mapping, see the [schema management guide](kafka/guides/schema-management).\n\n### Message size limits\n\nTinybird has a default message size limit of 10 MB. Messages exceeding this limit are sent to the Quarantine Data Source. For strategies on handling large messages and troubleshooting quarantined messages, see the [message size handling guide](kafka/guides/message-size-handling).\n\n## Kafka .datasource settings\n\n{% table %}\n   * Instruction\n   * Required\n   * Description\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_CONNECTION_NAME`\n   * Yes\n   * Name of the configured Kafka connection in Tinybird. It must match the name of the\n     connection file (without the extension).\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_TOPIC`\n   * Yes\n   * Name of the Kafka topic to consume from.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_GROUP_ID`\n   * Yes\n   * Consumer Group ID to use when consuming from Kafka.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_AUTO_OFFSET_RESET`\n   * No\n   * Offset to use when no previous offset can be found, like when creating a new consumer. Supported values are `latest` and `earliest`. Default: `latest`.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_STORE_HEADERS`\n   * No\n   * Adds a `__headers Map(String, String)` column to the data source, and stores Kafka headers in it for later processing. Default value is `False`.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_STORE_RAW_VALUE`\n   * No\n   * Stores the raw message in its entirety in the `__value` column. Default: `False`.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_KEY_FORMAT`\n   * No\n   * Format of the message key. Valid values are `avro`, `json_with_schema`, and `json_without_schema`. Using `avro` or `json_with_schema` requires `KAFKA_SCHEMA_REGISTRY_URL` to be set in the connection file used by the data source.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_VALUE_FORMAT`\n   * No\n   * Format of the message value. Valid values are `avro`, `json_with_schema`, and `json_without_schema`. Using `avro` or `json_with_schema` requires `KAFKA_SCHEMA_REGISTRY_URL` to be set in the connection file used by the data source.\n{% /table %}\n\n## Kafka .connection settings\n\n{% table %}\n   * Instruction\n   * Required\n   * Description\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS`\n   * Yes\n   * Comma-separated list of one or more Kafka brokers, including Port numbers.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL`\n   * Yes\n   * Security protocol for the connection. Accepted values are `PLAINTEXT` and `SASL_SSL`. Default value is `SASL_SSL`.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SASL_MECHANISM`\n   * No\n   * SASL mechanism to use for authentication. Supported values are `PLAIN`, `SCRAM-SHA-256`, `SCRAM-SHA-512`, `OAUTHBREARER`. Default value is `PLAIN`.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_KEY`\n   * When using SASL `PLAIN` or `SCRAM`\n   * Sometimes called Key, Client Key, or Username depending on the Kafka distribution.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SECRET`\n   * When using SASL `PLAIN` or `SCRAM`\n   * Sometimes called Secret, Secret Key, or Password depending on the Kafka distribution.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_METHOD`\n   * When using SASL `OAUTHBEARER`\n   * Currently only `AWS` is supported.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_AWS_REGION`\n   *  When using SASL `OAUTHBEARER`\n   * AWS MSK cluster region.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_AWS_ROLE_ARN`\n   *  When using SASL `OAUTHBEARER`\n   * AWS role ARN to assume.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SASL_OAUTHBEARER_AWS_EXTERNAL_ID`\n   *  When using SASL `OAUTHBEARER`\n   * External ID used when assuming the role.\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SCHEMA_REGISTRY_URL`\n   * No\n   * URL of the Kafka schema registry. Used for `avro` and `json_with_schema` deserialization of\n     keys and values. If Basic Auth is required, include credentials in the URL format:\n     `https://\u003cusername\u003e:\u003cpassword\u003e@\u003cregistry_host\u003e`\n   ---\n   * `KAFKA_SSL_CA_PEM`\n   * No\n   * Content of the CA certificate in PEM format for SSL connections. [Multiline setting](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles#multiple-lines)\n{% /table %}\n\n## AWS IAM permissions\n\nTo grant Tinybird access to your Kafka cluster, you must create an AWS IAM role with two policies: an access policy and a trust policy.\n\n### Manual configuration\n{% tabs variant=\"code\" initial=\"AWS Access Policy\" %}\n{% tab label=\"AWS Access Policy\" %}\n```json\n{\n    \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n    \"Statement\": [\n        {\n            \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n            \"Action\": [\n                \"kafka-cluster:Connect\",\n                \"kafka-cluster:AlterCluster\",\n                \"kafka-cluster:DescribeCluster\"\n            ],\n            \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:kafka:\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_REGION\u003e:\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_ACCOUNT_ID\u003e:cluster/\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_NAME\u003e/*\"\n        },\n        {\n            \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n            \"Action\": [\n                \"kafka-cluster:DescribeTopic\",\n                \"kafka-cluster:CreateTopic\",\n                \"kafka-cluster:WriteData\",\n                \"kafka-cluster:ReadData\"\n            ],\n            \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:kafka:\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_REGION\u003e:\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_ACCOUNT_ID\u003e:topic/\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_NAME\u003e/*/\u003cKAFKA_TOPIC\u003e\"\n        },\n        {\n            \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n            \"Action\": [\n                \"kafka-cluster:AlterGroup\",\n                \"kafka-cluster:DescribeGroup\"\n            ],\n            \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:kafka:\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_REGION\u003e:\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_ACCOUNT_ID\u003e:group/\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_NAME\u003e/*/\u003cKAFKA_GROUP\u003e\"\n        }\n    ]\n}\n```\n{% /tab %}\n{% tab label=\"AWS Trust Policy\" %}\n```json\n{\n    \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n    \"Statement\": [\n        {\n            \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n            \"Action\": \"sts:AssumeRole\",\n            \"Principal\": {\n                \"AWS\": \"arn:aws:iam::\u003cTINYBIRD_ACCOUNT_ID\u003e:root\"\n            },\n            \"Condition\": {\n                \"StringEquals\": {\n                    \"sts:ExternalId\": \"\u003cEXTERNAL_ID\u003e\"\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    ]\n}\n```\n{% /tab %}\n- `\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_REGION\u003e`: AWS region where the MSK cluster is located (for example, `us-east-1`).\n- `\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_ACCOUNT_ID\u003e`: AWS account identifier of the MSK cluster.\n- `\u003cMSK_CLUSTER_NAME\u003e`: Name of the MSK cluster (for example, `demo-cluster-1`).\n- `\u003cKAFKA_TOPIC\u003e`: Name of the Kafka topic to give read access. Use `*` to allow all topics.\n- `\u003cKAFKA_GROUP\u003e`: Name of the consumer group to give read access. Use `*` to allow all groups.\n- `\u003cTINYBIRD_ACCOUNT_ID\u003e`:\n  - For Tinybird Cloud environments: Tinybird's AWS account ID, which varies depending on your region and provider\n  - For Local environments: The AWS account ID of the credentials you pass to the Docker container with `--use-aws-creds`\n- `\u003cEXTERNAL_ID\u003e`: A unique identifier for your connection.\n\n### Get the configuration from the API\nCheck [current Tinybird regions](/api-reference#current-tinybird-regions) to see the available regions and their corresponding API endpoints.\n\n- Access Policy: `/v0/integrations/kafka/policies/read-access-policy`\n  - Use the `msk_cluster_arn` paramter to limit the access to only one MSK cluster.\n  - Use the `topics` parameter to limit the access to a list topics (comma separated).\n  - Use the `groups` parameter to limit the access to a list of consumer groups (comma separated).\n- Trust Policy: `/v0/integrations/kafka/policies/trust-policy`\n  - Use the connection name in the `external_id_seed` parameter\n\n{% /tabs %}\n\n## Kafka connector in the local environment\n\nYou can use the Kafka connector in the [Tinybird Local container](/forward/install-tinybird/local) to consume messages from a local Kafka server or a Kafka server in the cloud.\n\nFor detailed local development setup instructions, including Docker Compose examples and environment management, see the [local development guide](kafka/guides/local-development).\n\n### Local Kafka server with Docker Compose\n\nWhen using a local Kafka server, ensure the Tinybird Local container can access it. If you are running Kafka using Docker, Docker Compose is the best option to set up both Kafka and Tinybird Local in the same network. Here's an example using `apache/kafka`:\n\n```yaml\nnetworks:\n  kafka_network:\n    driver: bridge\n\nvolumes:\n  kafka-data:\n\nservices:\n\n  tinybird-local:\n    image: tinybirdco/tinybird-local:latest\n    container_name: tinybird-local\n    platform: linux/amd64\n    ports:\n      - \"7181:7181\"\n    networks:\n      - kafka_network\n\n  kafka:\n    image: apache/kafka:latest\n    hostname: broker\n    container_name: broker\n    ports:\n      - 9092:9092\n    environment:\n      KAFKA_BROKER_ID: 1\n      KAFKA_PROCESS_ROLES: \"broker,controller\"\n      KAFKA_CONTROLLER_QUORUM_VOTERS: \"1@broker:29093\"\n      KAFKA_CONTROLLER_LISTENER_NAMES: \"CONTROLLER\"\n      KAFKA_LISTENER_SECURITY_PROTOCOL_MAP: PLAINTEXT:PLAINTEXT,PLAINTEXT_HOST:PLAINTEXT,CONTROLLER:PLAINTEXT\n      KAFKA_ADVERTISED_LISTENERS: PLAINTEXT://kafka:29092,PLAINTEXT_HOST://localhost:9092\n      KAFKA_LISTENERS: PLAINTEXT://0.0.0.0:29092,PLAINTEXT_HOST://0.0.0.0:9092,CONTROLLER://0.0.0.0:29093\n      KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1\n      KAFKA_AUTO_CREATE_TOPICS_ENABLE: \"true\"\n    volumes:\n      - kafka-data:/var/lib/kafka/data\n    networks:\n      - kafka_network\n```\n\n### Network configuration\n\nThe key points about the network configuration:\n\n1. The example uses a bridge network (`kafka_network`) to allow communication between containers\n2. The Kafka service exposes ports for both internal container communication and external access\n3. Tinybird Local connects to Kafka using the internal network address\n4. The bootstrap servers address in your Kafka Connection should match the `KAFKA_ADVERTISED_LISTENERS` in the `docker-compose.yml` file (for example, `kafka:29092`)\n\n### Creating the Kafka connection and data source\n\nThe following examples use default values in the `tb_secret()` function, which are suitable for this local setup. When deploying to Tinybird Cloud, you set these secrets in the Tinybird Cloud environment instead.\n\nConnection file `/connections/kafka_conn.connection`\n\n```tb {% title=\"/connections/kafka_conn.connection\" %}\nTYPE kafka\nKAFKA_BOOTSTRAP_SERVERS {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SERVER\", \"kafka:29092\") }}\nKAFKA_SECURITY_PROTOCOL {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SECURITY_PROTOCOL\", \"PLAINTEXT\") }}\nKAFKA_SASL_MECHANISM {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_PROD_SASL_MECHANISM\", \"PLAIN\") }}\nKAFKA_KEY {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_KEY\", \"key\") }}\nKAFKA_SECRET {{ tb_secret(\"KAFKA_SECRET\", \"secret\") }}\n```\n\nA Schemaless kafka data source file `/datasources/kafka_ds.datasource`\n\n```tb {% title=\"datasources/kafka_ds.datasource\" %}\nSCHEMA \u003e\n    `data` String `json:$`\n\nKAFKA_CONNECTION_NAME kafka_conn\nKAFKA_TOPIC sample-topic\nKAFKA_GROUP_ID my_group_id\n```\n\n### Usage example\n\n{% steps %}\n\n#### Start the Docker containers\n\n```bash\ndocker compose up\n```\n\n#### Create the `sample-topic`\n\n```bash\ndocker exec -it broker /opt/kafka/bin/kafka-topics.sh --create --topic sample-topic --bootstrap-server localhost:9092\n\n# Created topic sample-topic.\n```\n\n#### Deploy the project\n\n```bash\ntb deploy\n# Running against Tinybird Local\n\n# * Changes to be deployed:\n# ------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# | status | name       | type       | path                              |\n# ------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# | new    | kafka_ds   | datasource | datasources/kafka_ds.datasource   |\n# | new    | kafka_conn | connection | connections/kafka_conn.connection |\n# ------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# * No changes in tokens to be deployed\n\n# Deployment URL: http://cloud.tinybird.co/local/7181/None/deployments/1\n\n# * Deployment submitted\n# » Waiting for deployment to be ready...\n# ✓ Deployment is ready\n# » Removing old deployment\n# ✓ Old deployment removed\n# » Waiting for deployment to be promoted...\n# ✓ Deployment #1 is live!\n# A deployment with no data is useless. Learn how to ingest at https://www.tinybird.co/docs/forward/get-data-in\n```\n\n#### Send data to the topic and query it\n\n```bash\necho '{\"data\": \"test\"}' | docker exec -i broker /opt/kafka/bin/kafka-console-producer.sh --topic sample-topic --bootstrap-server localhost:9092\n\ntb sql \"select * from kafka_ds\"\n# Running against Tinybird Local\n#   data               __value   __topic                  __partition   __offset   __timestamp           __key\n#   String             String    LowCardinality(String)         Int16      Int64   DateTime              String\n# ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n#   {\"data\": \"test\"}             sample-topic                       0          1   2025-06-20 12:17:49\n```\n\n{% /steps %}\n\n### Docker Compose troubleshooting\n\nIf you encounter connection issues:\n\n1. Ensure all containers are running: `docker-compose ps`\n2. Check container logs: `docker-compose logs kafka`\n3. Ensure the bootstrap servers address in your Connection file matches the `KAFKA_ADVERTISED_LISTENERS` value in your `docker-compose.yml` file.\n\n## Kafka meta columns\n\nWhen you connect a data source to Kafka, the following columns are added to store metadata from Kafka messages:\n\n{% table %}\n   * name\n   * type\n   * description\n   ---\n   * `__value `\n   * `String`\n   * A String representing the entire unparsed value of the Kafka message. It is only populated if `KAFKA_STORE_RAW_VALUE` is set to `True`.\n   ---\n   * `__topic `\n   * `LowCardinality(String)`\n   * The topic that the message was read from.\n   ---\n   * `__partition `\n   * `Int16`\n   * The partition that the message was read from.\n   ---\n   * `__offset `\n   * `Int16`\n   * The offset of the message.\n   ---\n   * `__timestamp `\n   * `Datetime`\n   * The timestamp of the message.\n   ---\n   * `__key `\n   * `String`\n   * The key of the message.\n{% /table %}\n\n\nOptionally, when `KAFKA_STORE_HEADERS` is set to `True`, the following column is added and populated:\n{% table %}\n   * name\n   * type\n   * description\n   ---\n   * `__headers`\n   * `Map(String, String)`\n   * Kafka headers of the message.\n{% /table %}\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nWhen you iterate your Kafka data source, you might need to use the meta columns in the\n[FORWARD_QUERY](/forward/test-and-deploy/evolve-data-source#forward-query). Tinybird suggests a valid forward query that you can tweak to get the desired values for each column.\n{% /callout %}\n\n## Kafka logs\n\n{% snippet title=\"kafkalogs\" /%}\n\nFor comprehensive monitoring of your Kafka connectors, including lag tracking, throughput analysis, and error monitoring, see [Monitor Kafka connectors](/forward/monitoring/kafka-clickhouse-monitoring).\n\n## Pause and resume ingestion\n\nIn branches and Tinybird Local, you can pause and resume Kafka ingestion using the CLI:\n\n```bash\ntb [--branch=BRANCH_NAME] datasource stop my_kafka_datasource\ntb [--branch=BRANCH_NAME] datasource start my_kafka_datasource\n```\n\nStopping a Data Source pauses ingestion from the Kafka topic. When you start it again, the behavior depends on the environment. In branches, a new consumer group is created and ingestion starts from the latest offset. In Tinybird Local, ingestion resumes from the last committed offset.\n\n{% callout type=\"info\" %}\nBecause each start creates a new consumer group, previous consumer groups become orphaned. Depending on your Kafka cluster's consumer group TTL (`offsets.retention.minutes`), these orphan groups may persist until they expire.\n{% /callout %}\n\nSee [tb datasource start](/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-datasource#tb-datasource-start) and [tb datasource stop](/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-datasource#tb-datasource-stop) for more details.\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\nFor comprehensive troubleshooting guidance, see the [Kafka connector troubleshooting guide](kafka/troubleshooting).\n\nCommon issues include:\n- Connection timeout or broker unreachable\n- Authentication failures\n- SSL/TLS certificate validation errors\n- Deserialization errors (Avro, JSON)\n- Offset and consumer group conflicts\n- Consumer lag issues\n- Schema mismatches\n\nEach combination of `KAFKA_TOPIC` and `KAFKA_GROUP_ID` can only be used in one data source,\notherwise the offsets committed by the consumers of different data sources clash.\n\nIf you connect a data source to Kafka using a `KAFKA_TOPIC` and `KAFKA_GROUP_ID` that were\npreviously used by another data source in your workspace, the data source only receives data\nfrom the last committed offset, even if `KAFKA_AUTO_OFFSET_RESET` is set to `earliest`.\n\nTo prevent these issues, always use unique `KAFKA_GROUP_ID`s when testing Kafka data sources.\n\nSee [Kafka logs](#kafka-logs) to learn how to diagnose any other issues\n\n### Compressed messages\n\nTinybird can consume from Kafka topics where Kafka compression is turned on; decompressing the\nmessage is a standard function of the Kafka consumer. However, if you compressed the message before passing it through the Kafka producer, Tinybird can't do post-consumer processing to decompress the message.\n\nFor example, if you compressed a JSON message through gzip and produced it to a Kafka topic as a\n`bytes` message, it would be ingested by Tinybird as `bytes`. If you produced a JSON message to a\nKafka topic with the Kafka producer setting `compression.type=gzip`, while it would be stored in\nKafka as compressed bytes, it would be decoded on ingestion and arrive to Tinybird as JSON.\n\n## Connecting an existing data source to Kafka\n\nYou can connect an existing, default data source to Kafka.\n\nCreate the Kafka .connection file if it does not exist, add the desired Kafka settings to the .datasource file, and add a [`FORWARD_QUERY`](/forward/test-and-deploy) to provide default values for the [Kafka meta columns](#kafka-meta-columns).\n\n## Disconnecting a data source from Kafka\n\nTo disconnect a data source from Kafka, remove the Kafka settings from the .datasource file.\n\nIf you want to keep any of the [Kafka meta columns](#kafka-meta-columns), add them to the schema with a default value and adjust the `FORWARD_QUERY` accordingly.\n\n## Additional resources\n\n### Guides\n\n- [Confluent Cloud setup](kafka/guides/confluent-cloud-setup) - End-to-end setup for Confluent Cloud\n- [AWS MSK setup](kafka/guides/aws-msk-setup) - Complete MSK configuration guide\n- [Redpanda setup](kafka/guides/redpanda-setup) - Redpanda-specific configuration\n- [Local development](kafka/guides/local-development) - Local development setup and testing\n- [CI/CD and version control](kafka/guides/cicd-version-control) - Managing connections across environments\n- [Schema management](kafka/guides/schema-management) - Schema evolution and data type mapping\n- [Partitioning strategies](kafka/guides/partitioning-strategies) - Best practices for Kafka partitioning\n- [Message size handling](kafka/guides/message-size-handling) - Handling large messages and troubleshooting\n- [Performance optimization](kafka/guides/performance-optimization) - Throughput optimization and tuning\n\n### Reference\n\n- [Troubleshooting guide](kafka/troubleshooting) - Comprehensive error resolution with error lookup table\n- [Limits and quotas](kafka/limits) - Kafka connector limits and how to request increases\n\n### Related documentation\n\n- [Monitor Kafka
